Detained Rice Boats Not Released Yesterday, Wusong River Traffic Blocked

*Dagon News* reports: The rice markets in the Zhabei, Xinzha Bridge, and North Suzhou River areas of this city have been cut off from supplies because rice boats from Wuxi, Changshu, Kunshan, Suzhou, Jiangyin, and other inland areas being transported to Shanghai have been detained by the Jiwangmiao police station in Jiading County. It has been three days and they have not been released, causing a sudden disruption of rice supply. All shops uniformly closed their doors yesterday morning, awaiting a resolution. The Wusong River, from Huangdu in the east to Beixinjing, is shallow and crowded with parked rice boats, completely blocking traffic.

Limited Rice Reserves

Due to the influence of the Shanghai North Rice Market, rice prices in the South Rice Market suddenly soared. The prices of rice in the upper and middle grades uniformly rose by 2 to 4 jiao the day before yesterday. When trading opened yesterday morning, prices rose again by more than 2 jiao. The prices of local rice have also risen. According to a reporter's investigation, the rice reserves in Shanghai, in the warehouses and shops in Pudong in the south of the city, are only over 200,000 dan. The reserves of milled rice in the north of the city are less than 10,000 dan. If the detained rice boats are not released, there will be panic in Shanghai's food supply, and prices will likely skyrocket.

General Meeting

The Bean and Rice Trade Association is scheduled to hold an emergency meeting of all rice merchants in the city at 2:00 PM today at Cuixiu Hall on Fuyou Road to discuss countermeasures. Representatives will be sent to the Jiangsu Provincial Government and the Department of Civil Affairs, together with representatives from the Municipal Chamber of Commerce, the Local Association, the Shanghai North Rice Merchants Association, and the Changshu Association, to request consideration and demand immediate release in order to maintain the food supply of Shanghai citizens.

Flour and Wheat Market Continues to Rise Yesterday, Exchange Establishes Supplementary Trading Measures

The flour and wheat market in this city has recently been manipulated by speculators and affected by the current situation, resulting in severe fluctuations. Yesterday, the flour and wheat market continued to rise. In order to stabilize market transactions, the Flour Exchange, in addition to the regulations stipulated in the original operating rules, established supplementary measures. The details are as follows:

Exchange Notice

Yesterday, the Shanghai Flour Exchange issued a notice to stabilize market transactions, stating: "For the purpose of announcement, the shareholders' meeting on August 30th of this year entrusted the board of directors to handle the case of canceling public warehouses proposed by shareholders Zhang Weiyun and others. After soliciting opinions from various parties, the board of directors decided to continue to operate in accordance with Article 71 of the exchange's operating rules from January 26th, and to set additional supplementary measures as follows. Special announcement: (1) The delivery of forward contracts shall still be governed by Article 71 of the exchange's operating rules, but the exchange shall decide one month before the daily delivery whether the delivery on that day shall be applicable to the warehouse receipts of the warehouses prepared or designated by the exchange, or to the factory warehouse receipts, and announce it in the market. (2) For those delivered by factory warehouse receipts decided by the exchange, the buying broker shall still pay the price according to the exchange's usual practice (ten-day bank drafts or bank drafts approved by the exchange) and hand the factory warehouse receipts to the buying broker, who shall pick up the goods within ten days. The selling broker shall hand the factory warehouse receipts to the exchange, which shall issue a receipt and pay the delivery money on schedule within ten days. (3) The buying broker shall clear all the goods within ten days from the date of delivery of the factory warehouse receipts obtained at delivery. The exchange shall not be liable for any consequences if the goods are not delivered on time. (4) For those decided by the exchange to be delivered by the warehouse receipts of the self-provided or designated warehouses, the payment of money and goods shall still be handled in accordance with the regulations in the latter paragraph of Article 71 of the exchange's operating rules."

Yesterday's Rising Trend

Yesterday, the prices of flour in various months all rose. The recent market price broke the record of four yuan again, reaching four yuan and four fen, while the distant price reached four yuan and five jiao. This rising trend is indeed rare in recent years. As for wheat, due to buying by merchants and chasing by short sellers, the rising trend did not subside. The market price at the close was one jiao higher than the day before. Due to price limits, it could not go higher, so it is expected that it will be difficult to see a low price in the short term.

College Student Dances with Woman, Steals Camera, Because Dancer Will Soon Give Birth, Camera Was Stolen and Pawned for Money

Zhang Baocheng, a fifth-year student at Soochow Law School, founded a Guoguang News Agency at No. 8 Xiangkang Lane, Meibaige Road. On the 25th of last month, Wu Guoxiong (24 years old), a former second-year student from Soochow, visited Zhang Baocheng. Zhang treated Wu generously as a former classmate, and they had a long conversation. For two consecutive days, until 3:50 PM on the 27th, Wu visited Zhang again. At that time, Zhang was out, and Zhang's classmate, Zhou Zhen, entertained him. Later, Zhou had to go out as well, so he asked Wu to stay temporarily in the office outside the bedroom, and locked the bedroom door. Unexpectedly, Wu Guoyou had a sudden change of heart. Seeing that no one was in the room, he used an iron tool to pry open the lock of the room and entered, stealing a camera worth 150 yuan, and fled without a trace. When Zhang Baocheng returned home and discovered that the camera was missing, he began to investigate. Later, according to the tea boy Ni Baozhang, he saw Wu Guoxiong carrying a black box in the alley when he returned to the agency that day. Only then did he realize that Wu had done it and immediately reported it to the Xinzha police station. As late as 4:00 PM the day before yesterday, Zhang Baocheng learned that Wu Guoxiong was currently in the Huaan Insurance Company on Jing'an Temple Road, so he informed the police to arrest him. Unexpectedly, Wu found out and took the opportunity to escape. Around 12:00 PM the night before, Zhang learned that Wu lived with a certain dancer at No. 60, Lane 7, Chengdu Road, so he reported to the police station and dispatched detectives to arrest Wu. Yesterday morning, he was sent to the Eighth Criminal Court of the First Special Court. Police lawyer Zhang Dayin prosecuted him for theft under Article 321, Paragraph 2 of the Criminal Law and presented the case. Zhang Baochong also testified to the above situation. The defendant Wu Guoxiong confessed, "I used to work at the Shanghai Trust Company, and I went to Soochow Law School at night, but then I dropped out. Since last month, I have been working as a street vendor for the Continental News Agency. This time, because the dancer I love is pregnant and about to give birth, I was in financial difficulties and resorted to this tactic. I have now pawned the camera at Chengan Pawnshop at No. 108 Wusong Road and spent all 43 yuan I received. Now the dancer has also come to court and is asking for forgiveness." After the interrogating judge verified the confession, he ordered the defendant to be detained and await the rescheduled hearing next Wednesday.

National Merchants Bureau Streamlines Hygiene on Ships, Issues Hygiene Implementation Measures

Since its reorganization, the state-run China Merchants Bureau has paid close attention to the hygiene and cleanliness of all cabins, including kitchens and toilets, on its ships. It has repeatedly ordered its ship captains to supervise their staff to thoroughly clean these areas. To prevent negligence over time or any improper practices, the bureau has issued hygiene implementation measures and instructed all ships to comply with them, aiming for systematic improvement and concrete actions. The implementation measures are excerpted as follows:

(1) Each ship shall designate one officer each from the navigation department and the business department, and one staff member to be specifically responsible for managing the overall hygiene of the ship. (2) Each ship shall conduct a major cleaning each time it arrives at its destination and returns to Shanghai, with the chief mate responsible for supervising the process. (3) For ease of inspection, the cleaning matters of each ship shall be divided into seven areas: 1. Special-class cabins; 2. Passenger cabins; 3. Deck area; 4. Business department; 5. Cargo handling department; 6. Engine room; 7. Chinese and Western kitchens. (4) Each area of each ship shall be equipped with the following appropriate sanitary utensils: 1. Fruit peel bins; 2. Spittoons; 3. Brooms, dustpans, and watering cans; (4) Toilets. In addition to existing equipment, additions can be designed and added as needed. (5) The sanitation of the kitchen shall be the responsibility of the contractor to supervise the Chinese and Western cooks, and attention should be paid to the following items: (1) All Chinese and Western cooks must have their hair cut short, wash their hair every two days, and get a haircut twice a month. (2) All Chinese and Western cooks must wear white coats and hats, which should be changed and washed daily. (3) Chinese and Western cooks should cut their fingernails at least once a week and bathe, once a day in hot weather and at least once each time in cold weather. (4) All utensils used in the kitchen should be disinfected and cleaned once a day after work, and wiped with boiling water. Knives, bowls, chopsticks, and porcelain basins should be used exclusively and not for other purposes, and should be placed in designated places and not left in disarray. (5) Kitchen cloths, wooden buckets, kitchen knives, and other cutting utensils must be cleaned after each use before being used again (it is advisable to prepare multiple sets). (6) The kitchen walls, floorboards, tables, stove shelves, etc., must be kept clean. They must be swept and wiped clean after each meal and must not be allowed to accumulate dirt or be used for sleeping. (7) Clean water should be used for washing seaweed and rice. Unclean or rotten vegetables should be discarded immediately. (8) The kitchen should have plenty of gauze covers or gauze cabinets for storing dishes. (6) The hygiene of the special-class cabins, senior crew rooms, toilets, and bathrooms shall be the responsibility of the manager to supervise, and attention should be paid to the following items: 1. The special-class cabin stewards should follow the first three items of the preceding article. However, uniforms do not need to be changed daily. 2. Single quilts, pillowcases, bed sheets, etc., that come into contact with passengers' bodies must be changed and washed after each passenger uses them. Tablecloths and chair covers should be changed and washed immediately if they appear dirty, but at least every half month. 4. Each room should be cleaned once a day and thoroughly cleaned after arriving at the port, and should be swept and kept clean at all times. 5. Bathtubs, flush toilets, spittoons, washbasins, teaware, and tableware should be kept clean at all times and wiped clean at least once a day. Glass windows and copper objects, and lampshades should be wiped clean daily. (7) The hygiene of cabins of all classes (except special class), toilets, and bathrooms shall be the responsibility of the stewards of each zone to supervise (the number of zones shall be determined by each ship at its discretion). 1. The hygiene of the stewards shall be handled with reference to the first two items of Article 5. However, uniforms do not need to be changed daily. 2. For the cleaning of cabins and all utensils, refer to the last item of Article 6. Passenger cabin mattresses should be sunned twice a month. 3. Hallways, handrails, and fourth-class passenger areas on both sides of the ship should be swept by two stewards rotating every half hour. If bins are provided, they should be washed at all times. 4. Each toilet stall in third- and fourth-class cabins should be separated by a spring door and equipped with a porcelain basin for passengers to wash. (8) The hygiene of officers' rooms and offices shall be the responsibility of the officers to supervise the workers, in accordance with the preceding article. (9) The cleaning of the engine room shall be the responsibility of the chief engineer to supervise the workers. (10) The cleaning of the deck area shall be the responsibility of the boatswain to supervise the sailors to wash it once a day and to wash the entire ship once after arriving at the port. (11) If passengers spit indiscriminately or litter, the stewards should kindly advise them. If they do not listen, they should report to the hygiene officer in charge for peaceful handling. (12) If a patient is found on board, whether employee or passenger, the hygiene officer in charge should be notified immediately for treatment and isolation. If the disease is very serious or has the possibility of spreading, the branch office should be notified after arriving at the next port and sent to the local hospital, and disinfection work should be carried out immediately in the patient's residence. (13) For routine disinfection work on each ship, at least once per voyage in spring and summer, and at least once per month in autumn and winter. (14) The hygiene officers assigned to each ship shall stipulate the matters to be inspected daily as follows: 1. Personal hygiene inspection of stewards and cooks, once each in the afternoon every day. 2. Kitchen hygiene inspection, once per meal, and a major inspection at night. 3. Toilet and bathroom inspection once a day. 4. Regular patrols of other areas, with at least one formal inspection every day. 5. Full ship inspection after major cleaning upon arrival at port. (15) In addition to routine daily inspections, the captain shall conduct at least one inspection per voyage and one inspection after the major cleaning upon arrival at port. Business personnel should also participate in this inspection. (16) The inspection may be carried out in conjunction with the new transportation guidance officer. If any discrepancies are found, they should be corrected immediately. If they are not corrected after correction, they should be reported to the Bureau for review. (17) When holding general manager memorial weeks or spiritual lectures on board, the ship's overall hygiene work should be raised at any time to guide improvement methods. (18) Each ship may formulate detailed implementation measures for hygiene work based on its own situation and issue them by order of the captain. (19) If there are any omissions in these measures, the ship captains may submit opinions to the Bureau for revision.

Two Theaters Today Screen Films to Celebrate the Dedication of Aircraft

The central photography department's short film dedicated to celebrating the donation of aircraft was brought to Shanghai by a member sent by the central propaganda minister a month ago and handed over to various theaters for screening. It has been a long time since then, and the Da Guangming and Nanjing theaters have not yet screened it. Section Chief Wu of the Central Propaganda Department therefore came to Shanghai in person to inquire. After being contacted by Section Chief Li Dachao of the municipal government, it is now heard that the Nanjing and Da Guangming theaters have decided to add the film to their day and night shows today (the 5th), while the Da Shanghai and International Thai theaters will screen it tomorrow (the 6th).

Wu Qinmu Painting Exhibition

Wu Qinmu from Wujiang specializes in painting. He once stayed at Xu Qi Pang's residence, observing famous paintings for more than a year. His works all capture the spirit of the Tang, Song, Yuan, and Ming dynasties. Now, he is exhibiting more than 100 of his finest works at the Hushe Hall at the intersection of Beijing Road and Guizhou Road, scheduled for December 5th to 7th for two days. Those who are interested in calligraphy and painting can feast their eyes.

Yang Weiquan's Calligraphy and Painting Are Increasing in Value

The "Jinhui Dui" (pile of brocade ashes) painted by famous calligrapher and painter Yang Weiquan are exquisitely and realistically depicted. Famous figures of the time all praised them. The original price was 10 yuan per foot, and the fan face was 10 yuan per piece. In the year of Guiyou, it was increased by 20%, and in the year of Bingzi, it was increased by another 20%. However, those who love his works are still willing to pay heavily and compete to ask for paintings. This is because Mr. Yang never perfunctorily brushes off his work due to being too busy. Each painting takes five or six days, or more than ten days of work, and he must imitate it to the fullest extent so that the requesters are satisfied. Therefore, paper pieces are piled up like a mountain and he is overwhelmed. It is said that he is still burying himself in work all day long to meet the demand.

Baby Face Lives Up to Its Name

"Baby Face," sold by the French-Chinese Pharmacy, is the only skin-beautifying and moisturizing agent, and can be called the leading cosmetic product. Its function is not only to remove spots and moles, but also to change the appearance of the skin. Therefore, once applied, it is bright, tender, radiant, and the same as the innocent face of a baby. The name "Baby Face" truly lives up to its name.

Ministry of Finance Issues an Order to Exempt Chinese Oil Lamps from Tax

The pressure vegetable oil lamps produced by the China Oil Lamp Company at 218 Shandong Road in this city are designed to burn domestic vegetable oil. Not only are they exquisitely produced and beautiful in form, but they are also of great importance to the people's livelihood. Since their release, they have been well received by the community. Previously, they were approved by the 188th meeting of the Executive Yuan to be exempted from export tax and transit tax and to reduce and exempt freight charges as an incentive, and were handed over to the Ministries of Finance, Industry, Communications, and Railways for handling separately. Now, the company has received a batch order No. 31441 from the Ministry of Finance, and it is known that the supervisors of each pass have been ordered to immediately exempt the tax by the taxation department.

Weather Report

The Xujiahui Observatory's weather forecast at 4:30 PM yesterday stated that the weather around Shandong and the Yellow Sea is clear and cold, with sandstorms or strong northwesterly winds. There are northwesterly winds in the Yellow River basin. The upper and middle reaches of the Yangtze River are clear with indefinite winds. The lower reaches of the Yangtze River are sometimes cold and sometimes cloudy, with fog and strong northwesterly winds. The East China Sea and Taiwan are clear with regular strong seasonal winds. The hurricane southeast of Macclesfield Island is still moving west-northwest. Its center reached within about 120 miles of 15 degrees north latitude and 119 degrees east longitude at 6:00 AM. The wind force is unknown. Also, within the 24 hours before 3:00 PM yesterday, the highest temperature in this city was 55.9 and the lowest was 26.6. On the same day last year, the highest was 44.8 and the lowest was 38.5.

Lying About Death to Obtain Compensation, Li Bingchang Sentenced, Li Detained for 50 Days, His Wife Sentenced to 30 Days

Li Bingchang (also known as Li Benchu), the owner of the Liyuan Money Shop in Huyang County, Guangdong, and a native of Shantou, took out a life insurance policy with American United Life Insurance Company for HK$50,000 in May 1932. However, Li had recently suffered business losses and the money shop had closed down. He came up with a bizarre idea and colluded with his wife, Li Liang Zhiying, to write a letter to United Life Insurance Company stating that Li Bingchang had committed suicide by drowning and demanding compensation of HK$50,000. After United Life Insurance Company learned that he was not actually dead, it sent a telegram to Li's family asking them to come to Shanghai for a face-to-face discussion. Li Liang Zhiying then came to Shanghai with her fellow villager Zhang Zhengde and stayed at the New Asia Hotel. Meanwhile, United Life Insurance Company's investigation revealed that Li Bingchang was hiding in Room 17 of the Lingnan Hotel on Wuchang Road. Based on this information, they reported to the General Police Department, which sent detectives to arrest Li Bingchang and Zhang Zhengde at the New Asia Hotel, and handed them over to the First Special Court. Police lawyer Qian Xunjiu prosecuted them for fraud under Article 339 of the Criminal Code. After an interrogation, the defendants were ordered to appear in court again on another day. Yesterday morning, under the continued interrogation of the three defendants by Judge Pan Zhenyang in the Criminal Court, Li Bingchang was sentenced to 50 days of detention for attempted joint fraud, Li Liang Zhiying was sentenced to 30 days of detention, and Zhang Zhengde was acquitted.

General Overview of Shanghai's Industrial and Commercial Changes in September 1936 (Continued)

— Edited by China Credit Information Agency

(Shanghai's Industrial and Commercial Overview - No. 39)

(3) Qinglian Pavilion Teahouse Transfer - This teahouse, which has eyes above it, has long been well-known. Since the old site was renovated and moved to the intersection of Hubei Road and Fuzhou Road, the owner of the building, Mr. Sun Furen, has actively reorganized it, and it has a completely new atmosphere. The interior is divided into a shopping mall and a small Guanghan theater. Recently, due to the impact of the depression, business has been sluggish. Mr. Sun has no intention of operating, so he transferred all the property, decoration, and trademarks to Dan Gui Company for operation, and added a note to show the distinction.

(4) Mother's Heart Hospital Opens - This hospital was founded by Mr. Lu Bohong, a wealthy industrialist and philanthropist in this city. Mr. Lu realized that the Zhabei area is vast, with a large number of residents, especially the poor. However, there are not many charitable hospitals suitable for them, and there are even fewer large-scale ones. Therefore, he opened up more than 20 acres of land near Niuqiao on Baoxing Road and started construction in early March of this year. The funds were from the gifts received by Mr. Lu during his 60th birthday celebration the year before last as a foundation, and he also received more than 2,000 yuan in donations from the municipal government and various charities. It was completed at the end of August. It is said that the total construction cost reached 70,000 yuan, and the internal equipment is complete and the scale is grand. It opened on the 26th of this month. It is said that the monthly recurring expenses are about 1,500 yuan or more, which are borne by Mr. Lu, the municipal government, the Nanshi Water and Electricity Company, the Huashang Tram Company, and the Inland Tap Water Company.

(5) Lido Company Founded - This company was converted from the residence of the wealthy Shanghai businessman Gan Yize. It includes a dance hall, a night garden, a hotel, and a swimming pool, with a large scope. The manager is Mr. Ma Jigan, who is good at dancing and has unlimited prospects.

In the manufacturing industry category, the number of new creations this month is the same as last month, and the number of closures is one less than last month. The general situation is very similar to last month, but the cotton textile industry has slightly improved due to the bumper cotton harvests in various places this year, the gradual decline in cotton prices, and the gradual increase in sales and prices of cotton yarn. The more important changes are described below.

(1) Hengfeng Textile Bureau Announces Resumption of Operations - This bureau is considered the originator of the textile industry in China. It was founded by Mr. Nie Yuntai as a sole proprietorship and was established in the sixteenth year of Guangxu, which is 46 years ago. The total capital is 1.15 million yuan and it is a limited company. The current factory director is Mr. Nie Lusheng. It has 514,506 yarn spindles, 611 looms, 800 horsepower of electricity, 100 horsepower of steam power, more than 3,300 workers, and more than 150 employees. It uses 76,000 dan of cotton and produces 22,000 bales of yarn and 10,360 square yards of cloth annually. The factory covers an area of more than 40 acres. Because of its novel architecture and scientific management, it has made great contributions to the history of the textile industry in China. At the beginning of the bureau's business, its operations gradually developed. Later, the outbreak of the European War brought the factory a lot of profit. Therefore, the scope was increasingly expanded. In addition to adding a second factory and a cloth factory, Mr. Nie also founded the Da Zhonghua Yarn Factory in Yunzaobang. Unexpectedly, the European War ended, British exchange rates rebounded, and foreign yarn was dumped. The factory suffered a blow and was almost shaken. I had to transfer the Da Zhonghua Factory to Yong'an Textile Company, and with the vigorous assistance of the banking community, it was finally saved from danger. In the following years, business was sluggish. It was not until 1925 that it saw a turnaround. It made a profit again between 1930 and 1931. However, since then, due to the depression in the market, purchasing power has become increasingly weak, and foreign goods have been dumped cheaply, it has fallen back into losses. It has tried its best to support itself for three years, with debts reaching more than 3 million yuan. Mr. Nie believes that if this continues, the future may be unimaginable. Therefore, he stopped work this spring, and it has been more than half a year. After autumn, due to the bumper cotton harvests in various places, the future of the yarn industry has shown a turnaround again. Therefore, after discussions between Zhejiang Xingye and Mr. Nie's plan, it was decided to lease the factory unconditionally to China Cotton Industry Trading Company for operation, for a period of three years. Mr. Nie resigned as the company's auditor and the consultant of China Cotton Company. Hu Huan of China Cotton Company will serve as the manager, and Wang Fuli will be hired as the associate and chief engineer. As for the company's previous debts to Zhejiang Xingye, interest payments will be suspended during the lease period. If there is a business profit, 5% will be taken as Mr. Nie's business micro-profit, and the remaining 95% will be split between Zhejiang Xingye China Cotton Company. If there is a loss, the China Cotton Company will be fully responsible. After the three parties signed an agreement, work was resumed on the 27th of this month. (To be continued)

Women's Special

How to Be a Revolutionary Woman?

— Tong Yizhen

For thousands of years, we have lived in darkness, political oppression, social contempt, and the shackles of Confucian etiquette such as "Women are not allowed to join political associations," "What do women and children know," and "A woman without talent is virtuous," which simply suffocated us. Since the vigorous "May Fourth Movement," it has directly set off the revolutionary wave of our "Women's Movement," shouting loudly for "freedom and equality!" But now it has been almost twenty years, what are our achievements? Alas! Many of our female compatriots are still bound in layers of darkness. In this view, I believe that we should be a revolutionary woman, embracing the ambition of "If I don't go to hell, who will?" to save them in the darkness. So how can we be a revolutionary woman? In my opinion, we should strive to implement several revolutionary conditions:

(1) Ideological Revolution - In ancient times, we have always been "governing the inner circle." Except for daily life and family duties, we don't ask or care about anything. I ask, if we continue like this, when will there be a day for us to "come out of the mountain"? The Western philosopher said, "Thought is the mother of enterprise." That's right, if we want to be revolutionary women and do a great cause, we should start with ideology. We must strive to break the corrupt ideas of the past few years and cultivate transcendent ideas.

(2) Revolution of Will - Our will is much weaker than others. After being tempted by the outside world, it is easy to change our original intentions, blindly follow, and be controlled by others. This is so dangerous! If we want to be revolutionary women, we must temper our will. Will can hold everything in our future. We must fill ourselves with courage and develop an indomitable perseverance to fight the environment!

(3) Habit Revolution - Our popular common problems, such as luxury, vanity, stinginess, jealousy, etc., are all the worst habits. Habits are the original elements of character, and these must be intentionally avoided. The habits we need are the spirit of enterprise and the魄strength of creation!

Female compatriots! Unite, we want to be revolutionary women. Vainly shouting slogans is useless. We should do it truly and practically! Especially in this extraordinary period, we must all embrace the determination of "If the country is not a country, how can there be a home?" and the悲愤 sorrow and indignation of "If the skin does not exist, what will the hair cling to?" We must work hard and revolutionize for ourselves and for the country!

Japanese Women Residing in Our Country

— A Single Hair

Although the number of Japanese residing in our country is not large, the composition is quite complex. Now, as the diplomatic relations between the two countries are being adjusted and unfortunate incidents are occurring in various places, we should have a special understanding of the Japanese women residing in the interior of our country.

Japanese women residing in our country can be roughly divided into three types. The first type is the family members of Japanese officials stationed in China or the families of large Japanese merchants. This category is small in number, usually lives a secluded life, and is not easy to approach. Their stay in our country is temporary, and they will return to their country in a short period. The second type is the women we often see, who are the families of legitimate small merchants. They themselves run shops, selling and managing, and are in a semi-permanent residence state. The third type is those who are not engaged in legitimate occupations or are engaged in secret professions. They can make their home anywhere, traveling between China and Japan without a fixed period of stay.

Women from the Kanto region around Tokyo are generally slender, with mostly oval faces. When they come to China, they are mostly the wives and daughters of officials and capitalists, with a high level of education and a great respect for their own personality. The Japanese women in the Hongkou area of North Sichuan Road in Shanghai, with high hairstyles and wearing wooden clogs, are the families of small merchants. After living here for a long time, they can speak a few words of Chinese, or at least understand Shanghai dialect. They are larger in stature than Tokyo people, with rough, dark skin and high cheekbones. These are people from Kyushu, Kobe, and Yokohama who could not develop in their own country and followed their husbands to our country to do business. If they have a comfortable life in our country and have no attachment to their hometown, they may never return to their homeland. They are familiar with the psychology of our people, and are very polite in their interactions with Chinese men and women, just as they treat their compatriots in their own country. Especially in receiving customers, their hospitality is even more skillful than that of our merchants. Although their level of knowledge is not high, their love for their country and their hometown is extremely strong. Although they live in our country, they still do not buy Chinese goods, and often live in groups. Therefore, wherever Japanese people live, there are Japanese shops selling Japanese goods. They only want to buy Japanese goods in Japanese shops and are unwilling to buy Japanese goods in Chinese shops. After giving birth to children in our country, they send them to relatives in Japan to receive education in their homeland after they graduate from elementary school. Therefore, unless they marry Chinese people, the children of ordinary merchants will never be assimilated by the Chinese.

Japanese women who are rootless and do not engage in legitimate occupations are especially numerous in Beijing and Shanghai. Their professions ultimately include dancers, prostitutes, masseuses, coffee girls, and wine servers. Their companions include merchants, soldiers, sailors, and vagrants, a complete mixture. Therefore, Japanese women who are immersed in secret lives all day long have an alluring and romantic attitude that is immediately recognizable. There are also those among our people who enjoy low-level entertainment, and it is very easy for unfortunate incidents to occur, which is harmful to international relations. Older women whose beauty and talent have declined have no choice but to engage in illicit activities to make a living. The Japanese magazine "Talk" in Tokyo reported that smuggling in North China and private buying of silver dollars in Shanghai were initially started by middle-aged, unscrupulous women. For the sake of national relations, women in both countries should respect themselves and others, and promote friendship and goodwill with each other.

Mrs. Roosevelt

— Wei Jing

Mrs. Roosevelt, the wife of the American President, will continue her life as the First Lady in the White House for another four years due to Mr. Roosevelt's re-election this year. Mrs. Roosevelt has many admirable words and deeds in her past four years in the White House that are worth mentioning. Here are some excerpts:

Although the Mrs. Roosevelt is the First Lady of the White House, she does not reduce her social engagements because of her high position. She still visits her female friends from before she became famous. In the White House, there are several hostel-like rooms specially set up for her female friends to come and stay for a short time. Therefore, her female friends, when they come, always stay for one or two weeks. Sometimes, when Mrs. Roosevelt is talking happily with her female friends, she will not return to her own bedroom and will spend the night in the same room with her female friends. If her female friends hold a banquet and invite Mrs. Roosevelt to participate, unless she is assisting her husband in handling important matters and is really unable to spare the time, she always personally attends the banquet, regardless of the cold or heat, distance or proximity. In January of last year, a female friend of hers in New York passed away, and the funeral was scheduled for 3:30 in the afternoon. Coincidentally, she was too busy to spare the time on the morning of that day, so she had to take a plane in the afternoon, carrying a wreath, and rush to New York to participate in the funeral. The weather that day was extremely bad, with wind and rain, but Mrs. Roosevelt did not stop her trip because of this. Her friendships are generally like this.

Liking children is one of Mrs. Roosevelt's habits. In the past four years, she has participated in the graduation ceremonies of elementary schools and awarded diplomas and prizes more than twenty times. She has participated in national children's sports meets more than ten times. She has participated in various amusement activities held by childcare organizations more than twenty times. She has traveled as far south as Florida and as far west as Arizona. This is a high record that previous First Ladies have never had in expressing their love for children. On Children's Day of the year before last and Christmas of last year, Mrs. Roosevelt took the opportunity of being at the White House to entertain children, preparing refreshments and toys, and having a great day. She is also very willing to help women. If there is an unemployed woman with a skill, she only needs to write a letter to Mrs. Roosevelt, and Mrs. Roosevelt will pay attention to it and look for a suitable position. It is said that in these four years, on average, a total of 354 to 400 people are introduced to positions that match their skills each year. Mrs. Roosevelt always replies to letters of complaint from old women who are poor and helpless, and comforts them, or sends letters to the state government to ask for help. Mrs. Roosevelt currently holds the position of writer for several publishing houses, and the income from her remuneration is entirely donated to several childcare organizations in the country. At the same time, the income from his real estate stocks is entirely donated to the old women in the country who have complained to her. It is said that in these four years, under these two items, a total of about 200,000 yuan is donated each year.

Mrs. Roosevelt is very proficient in cooking, and she also likes to do it herself. For daily banquets with guests and friends, half of the dishes are cooked by herself. If there is a large banquet, at least she has to make a dish herself to entertain the guests. The kitchen in the White House was built in 1887, but in 1933, Mrs. Roosevelt gathered several engineers to renovate it and create a state-of-the-art kitchen. From this point, we can also see Mrs. Roosevelt's attention to cooking.

These are the outlines of the life of the First Lady of the United States. It is said that in the past four years in the White House, Mrs. Roosevelt has lost about fifteen pounds. The wrinkles on her face have also deepened a lot. But her spirit is still so vigorous, because Mrs. Roosevelt's body is very healthy. It is said that in the past ten years, she has not been sick and bedridden for a single day.

Women's Issues in Folk Songs

— Ba Ling

"Little Sister Er, pushes a wheelbarrow to the north, can't push it, Fourth Brother sends her, sends her home, sits down and spins cotton, spins cotton until noon, mother-in-law gives her a bran cornbread, takes a bite, so sad, jump into the well, the well is too deep, jump into the river, the river is too high, clings to the riverbank and cries to the heavens!"

"The sun comes out with a pot of flowers, the cruel mother-in-law knows how to manage the house, when the daughter-in-law comes to cook, she grabs a handful of millet, first starts the fire, then cuts the vegetables, and quickly cooks the rice. The father-in-law and mother-in-law scoop thick rice, the daughter-in-law drinks vegetable soup, miserable, miserable, it's hard to be a daughter-in-law!"

"Pounding cloth stones, banging, I'll give you sixteen taels, ten fathers-in-law and one mother-in-law, ten sisters-in-law watching over me: watching me so that my toes don't touch the ground, taking a basket to fetch water, my feet are small, thin, and thin, my little feet are so painful, grasshoppers bite, chirp, chirp, I miss home, who knows? Lower my head and see the small gate of my mother's house; bend my waist and see the locust tree of my mother's house."

"Young girl, watch the imperial fair, walk a little, kneel a little; go home and cover yourself with a quilt, father-in-law beats, mother-in-law scolds, sister-in-law comes to pull your hair, pull one strand, ignore it, pull two strands, it hurts, pull three strands, jump into the river, the river is far away, jump into the well, the well is deep, clinging to the wellhead and scolding the matchmaker, matchmaker, you make money, I suffer, a gust of wind blows me back to my mother's house, look at my mother, leaning on a cane; look at my grandfather, wearing broken shoes; look at my sister, folding a quilt; look at my sister-in-law, folding a jacket; look at my brother, eating steamed buns and not letting me have any; cruel parents don't chase the dog, tear my skirt and bite my hand, angry young lady, hurry away."

The above four folk songs are very popular in northern China. In these four folk songs, we can consistently see the truth of the disharmony between mothers-in-law and daughters-in-law, and the pain of marriage and freedom. Those who care about women's happiness and lead the women's movement need to discuss this issue.

In the author's humble opinion, the fundamental problem to be solved in the above question lies in the lack of universal education for women. On the one hand, we hope that the education authorities will actively promote universal education so that everyone, regardless of gender, has the opportunity to receive a considerable education. At the same time, we especially hope that the leaders of the general women's circles will put forward this issue for research, set out a suitable solution, and conduct a large-scale publicity and campaign to attract the attention of the general public. Only then will there be a possibility of a solution. Such is my humble opinion, I wonder what the reader thinks?

Save Some Money on Cosmetics

Special Report of This Newspaper

Ms. Li Xiaqing Talks About Saving the Country Through Aviation

— Ji Ping

Building an Air Force is the Only Way to Gain a Foothold in the Future World. Prepare Early and Train Highly Skilled Personnel.

Saving the country through aviation is the unanimous call of compatriots across the country. At this time when the border bandits are tense and the war of resistance is fierce, enemy planes are rampant in our airspace, making us feel that aviation is truly the only weapon to save the country. In the past three or four years, with the enthusiastic promotion of the government and the people, aviation in our country has achieved considerable results, but it is still far behind the great powers. From now on, we must do our best to promote it, so that we can increase the strength of our national defense. According to the current situation, our country cannot supply itself with aircraft, talents cannot be universally trained, and gasoline cannot be mined in large quantities, which are indeed great obstacles to the development of the aviation industry. If we have a solution to these three items, then we can assert that China's aviation will not lag behind others. Here, focusing on the second item, the training of aviation talents is much more difficult than other technologies, and there are particularly few learners. In recent years, due to the deepening national crisis, young patriotic people have been more enthusiastic in joining the air force, which is a good phenomenon that promotes the prosperity of the country through adversity. However, there are still very few women learning aviation. Therefore, I believe that women learning aviation are outstanding heroines. A few months ago, after publishing an article on Yang Jinxun's aviation life, more than a dozen young women wrote to inquire about the content of the Flying Club, which is very interesting. Therefore, today I will introduce Ms. Li Xiaqing to the readers, and I believe it will arouse the deep sympathy of everyone.

(I)

Ms. Li is from Guangdong. She studied at St. Stephen's School in Hong Kong in her childhood, and later entered the Zhongxi Girls' High School in Shanghai. (She once worked as an actress in her father's Minxin Film Company, under the alias Li Dandan, but now she says that this is not worth recalling.) In 1928, she went to study in England for two years, and then went to Switzerland, where she lived in Geneva for four years. Half of the time was spent studying civil aviation at the Crendmerville Flying Club. After graduating, she went to the Boeing Flying School in the United States to study. The school is the most famous civil aviation school in the United States. Among the 150 students, she was the only woman. The curriculum was very heavy, from 8:00 in the morning to 5:00 in the evening, all focused on academic and technical subjects. Manufacturing, assembly, repair, and driving were all done. Astronomy, geography, radio, and other subjects were all available. Blind flight, dangerous flight, radio command, parachute, and other latest flying techniques were all learned. She said: "I have obtained two Swiss flight licenses and one American license. After returning to China, I passed the central examination and was also issued a license. Some people outside say that I cannot fly, which is really a joke. Since there is evidence of the fact, it seems unnecessary to argue more.

(II)

I asked her about the motivation for studying aviation. She said: "I like sports, which is more interesting than burying myself in front of the window. The "1918" and "January 28" incidents happened one after another. I lived far away in Switzerland and was greatly stimulated. Thinking of the enemy planes being so brutal, if we women want to serve the country, the only way is to study aviation. It is very similar to my own physical strength and interests. One is to show women's self-awareness and be able to advance with the times, and the other is that such a large motherland has no aviation construction (speaking four years ago), how can it gain a foothold in the scientific world? In fact, the navy is not easy to expand, and the army cannot exert its power without the cooperation of the air force. With such a long coastline, there is a danger of being controlled by the enemy at any time. Only by building an air force can we confront them with aircraft. If we women take the lead in advocating it, men will definitely not be willing to fall behind. So I strengthened my will."

(III)

"What are the numbers of female pilots in Europe and the United States, and which women are in China's aviation industry?" I thought she would know, so I asked this question. She thought for a while; "There are very few women in Europe and the United States who have contributed to the aviation industry, but the number of people engaged in learning is increasing day by day. There are no accurate statistics on the number of people. As far as I know, all major cities in the United States have Ninety-nine Clubs, (Ninety-nine club) membership is limited to women who have obtained a pilot's license. There are as few as 20 members and as many as 40 or 50 members. The total number in the United States is at least about 500 or more. The Soviet Union and Germany are next, and then England and France. In terms of technology, Soviet women are probably the most distinctive, because American women are all engaged in civil aviation, while Soviet women participate in military aviation. There are no more than six or seven women in our country who are studying flying, such as Li Yueying, Lin Pengxia, and Wang Canzhi, but unfortunately we have only studied it and have not been able to serve the country! Learning should be applied, and it is meaningless not to learn. Aviation is different from other academic disciplines. Learning or not learning is up to me, and using or not using is up to the government. At present, what the government needs is military aviation talents, and there are very few opportunities for those who study civil aviation. There are no third companies in the country other than Eurasia and China Airlines, and the need for talents is really limited, but I believe that the future will definitely be the world of aviation. To store villages for the country, we must prepare early. Once the technology is learned, heroes do not have to worry about not having a place to use their skills."

(IV)

"What are your opinions on this time of national crisis?" This question seemed to touch her patriotic heart. She talked incessantly for ten minutes, mainly saying, "In this critical autumn of survival for China, there is no distinction between men and women in serving the country. We must do our best. As women who have learned to fly, although we cannot be incorporated into the air force and go to the front line to kill the enemy, we can organize rescue teams and aerial transport teams in the air force to take care of the rear. I am preparing myself. Hongqiao and Longhua are places I often go to. Practicing flying is also a daily lesson. Once the government's conscription order comes, I will quickly rush to serve and be willing to be a pioneer. Recently, Ms. Yan Yaqing and I are launching a women's group, which aims to awaken women to advocate for the aviation industry. Women who do not know how to fly but are enthusiastic or interested in this are all welcome. As long as we can invite the central government to approve, we can proceed smoothly." Finally, she said that it is not impossible for women to learn aviation, but they must have a strong physique, sensitive hands and brains, a strong will, patience, and perseverance, and break through the family and social environment. The most important thing is the government's advocacy, encouragement, and the public's sympathy.

Ms. Li's Expression When Taking Off in Her Plane at Longhua (This Plane Was Made by the Naval Aircraft Manufacturing Bureau)

A Letter to Women Across the Country

— Xiao Bai

——Opinions on Assisting Suiyuan——

Dear Sisters:

I have been longing for an opportunity to communicate with you for a long time. However, I have never been able to do so. Now, because I have many very important things that I must talk to you about, I am humbly borrowing a corner of this garden to write this public letter to you:

At present, our country has clearly reached the final juncture, especially with the recent attack on Suiyuan by the puppet bandit army, which is trying to seize our only remaining first line of national defense, the barrier to North China and the Northwest. If we still have humanity, if we do not want to be obedient slaves of the enemy, then everyone feels that the only way forward is for each of our compatriots to bravely rise up and work hard to save ourselves. We women across the country account for half of the country's population, and we must never again adopt an attitude of watching the fire from the other side and hiding on the sidelines. We must join hands with men to set off a huge wave of national self-salvation and participate in and work hard in all work to assist Suiyuan.

Now, our loyal and brave soldiers on the front line have launched a heroic scene of defending the country in the war of resistance. For the sake of the mountains and rivers of the motherland and for the survival of the nation, they have been fighting bloody battles in the icy and snowy weather and in the midst of the flames of war. The recovery of Bai Lingmiao on the 24th is even more worthy of the greatest glory for the country and worthy of the infinite admiration of the people across the country.

The enthusiastic movement across the country to assist Suiyuan in the past two weeks is even more worthy of our joy and excitement. And our sisters have also organized rescue teams and raised donations to comfort the soldiers, which shows that our women are brave and decisive in their efforts to save the country. We also love the nation and the country in the same way, and have not forgotten the responsibilities that women should bear in the war of resistance.

Here, I would also like to put forward three more concrete and practical points to the women across the country on the current work to assist Suiyuan, because they are what we must do.

First, we should expand the rescue movement. Those of us who already understand rescue work should indeed find ways to go to the front line to rescue soldiers. Those of us who do not understand it should start learning, because that is the most important work for us women in the war of resistance.

Second, we must launch the work of sewing winter clothes and knitting woolen sweaters, because these are necessities for soldiers in the icy and snowy weather, and they are also our very urgent main work.

Third, we must work as hard as men to raise donations, and be able to solicit donations from our relatives and sisters.

In short, now is the time to roar. We don't want empty talk and loud shouts. We want everyone to do it practically! Sisters! I hope you will discuss, supplement, and implement it immediately.

Pei Yingli's Younger Brother

— Xue Ying

Oh, heartless heavens! Last night, when Pei Yingli returned from the factory, the path in the dark and wretched Caoxiebang area was bathed in silvery moonlight, and the air felt only faintly humid. Who would have thought that today it would start raining a steady, persistent drizzle!

Pei Ying woke up at five o'clock, not because of the thunder, but because the layers of sorrowful thoughts stirred in her heart, preventing her from falling back into a deep sleep. As soon as she woke up, the sound of rain outside the window drilled into her ears. She didn't need to open the window to know that it was a long-lasting rain that wouldn't stop anytime soon.

Using the red glow from the kerosene lamp, she glanced at a new piece of clothing folded on the table, and couldn't help but sigh deeply. She had saved six months' worth of snack money to make this new outfit. Although it wasn't made of leather, silk, velvet, or even lined, just a thin silk shirt, it had consumed countless thoughts from planning, cutting the fabric, to tailoring. However, this outfit wasn't for her to wear but was made for her younger brother. He was lying on the bed opposite her, his delicate and thin face filling her with more love and pity each time she looked at him. Since their father was brutally killed by the XX army in Guanwai, she had done everything in her power to help him graduate from elementary school, then enter middle school, and then graduate from middle school. She also kept her promise to make her brother a new outfit so he could wear it to take a photo with his classmates on graduation day.

Her brother was indeed obedient. Each semester, in addition to tuition, board, lodging, and books costing around eighty yuan, he rarely spent more than one yuan a month on pocket money. Moreover, his grades were excellent. Pei Ying loved him so much that she really wanted to grit her teeth and send him to high school. However, several relatives felt that Pei Ying was already suffering too much and advised her to quickly find someone to recommend her brother for a job. One of her uncles even clipped an advertisement for the telegraph office's recruitment of clerks. Pei Ying saw that the qualifications—middle school graduate, age 16 to 19, salary of 20 yuan per month—were all suitable. However, the application deadline was too tight: it was noon tomorrow, and tomorrow was not a Sunday, so taking leave from the factory would result in a deduction of pay. Pei Ying ignored this, hoping that her brother could apply and get into the telegraph office, where a monthly salary of 20 yuan would be a very fortunate start for a middle school graduate.

To apply, they had decided last night that he would wear the new outfit. Unexpectedly, the heartless heavens sent rain. Pei Ying now had no time to worry about whether her brother would pass the exam. Her attention was temporarily focused on the new outfit. "Don't let caring for the outfit cost your brother an opportunity." "Don't end up failing the exam and ruining the clothes." These two conflicting thoughts fought in her mind. In the end, she decided to let her brother wear the new outfit because she knew that people nowadays value appearance the most.

Her brother woke up at half past seven, unaware that his sister had been wrestling with these thoughts for more than two hours. When they were about to leave with rain gear, her brother saw that the rain outside was too heavy and was reluctant to wear the new outfit. He wanted to change into something else, but Pei Ying felt it was inappropriate. Although she let him change into an old outfit, she still wrapped the new one up and carefully tucked it under her waist along with the graduation certificate, as if carrying a precious jewel.

Near the telegraph office, Pei Ying found a secluded alley and helped her brother change into the new outfit herself. She repeatedly straightened his collar and hem before letting him walk into the telegraph office alone. By this time, many young people had gathered at the entrance to register. Pei Ying felt there were too many people, and her brother might not be able to register. Seeing that the rain was getting heavier and heavier, she worried that her brother's new clothes would be completely ruined this time. She waited at the alley entrance for what seemed like an eternity before finally seeing her brother running back, soaked to the bone. Without waiting for her to ask, he told her that he had registered. Immediately, a smile surged onto her face, but when her eyes fell on her brother's new clothes, which were covered in rainwater and mud, tears streamed down her face.

Shen Bao Local Supplement

Talk

National Government Issues Conscription Order

— Wen

The Ministry of Military Administration issued a proclamation that a conscription system would be implemented on a trial basis in the five provinces of Henan, Anhui, Jiangxi, Zhejiang, and Jiangsu. A sincere announcement to the people.

This conscription law, aimed at bolstering the nation's strength, should be followed without fail. China is currently facing a critical moment, the life of the entire nation dancing in the hands of death. Every Chinese citizen who is not a traitor and does not want to be a traitor is willing to contribute their last drop of blood to the country, to shed it to fight for the nation's final right to exist. Under such circumstances of unusually high anti-enemy sentiment, I believe that every citizen will give the government's conscription order the most enthusiastic support.

The government's conscription order, premised on resisting the enemy, will surely gain the most enthusiastic support of the entire populace. We know that when steel is heated to its melting point, if it is not immediately poured into a mold, it will cool and solidify. Reheating it would waste the coal and time spent melting it previously. There is also a taboo in the art of war called "an aging army." An aging army is one that fails to capitalize on its initial momentum to conquer the enemy's camp, instead prolonging the situation, allowing the enemy to calmly prepare their offensive strategies. Once the morale of our side's valiant soldiers is dampened, their courage will greatly diminish, doubts and disagreements will arise, and they will no longer be able to exert their strength together as they did in their prime. This is very basic common sense. But looking back at the current state of our national resistance against Japan, is it still at its peak? Consider the January 28th Incident. The people of the whole country, especially those living in the counties near Shanghai, supported the 19th Route Army with all their enthusiasm. At that time, in a certain county near Shanghai, an event remains unforgettable to me: a middle-aged woman with bound feet personally brought two large, round blocks of high-quality white sugar rice cakes (which they normally would not casually give away) to the "National Salvation Association," which served as the collection center for comfort items in that county, saying, "There is nothing else to send. My old mother told me to send these rice cakes." But we never went door-to-door to solicit donations, nor did we issue a single fundraising flyer. We only announced verbally that we were collecting comfort items to reward the 19th Route Army. On another occasion, the radio broadcast (since the Shanghai newspapers had stopped reporting) that there were already too many food items sent to the 19th Route Army, more than they could eat, and that they hoped to receive tens of thousands of pairs of straw sandals tied with hemp. The county did not have many straw sandals, and they were never stored in advance. Hemp-tied straw sandals were especially rare, but within two days and nights, they managed to rush-make and collect three thousand pairs. And consider the current nationwide movement, from top to bottom, unanimously supporting the officers and soldiers fighting in Suiyuan. How is it any different from the support given to the 19th Route Army in the past? This is precisely the "morale" of the entire nation, which is at its peak and cannot be obscured by any excuses!

Therefore, with the National Government issuing the conscription law, all of our citizens should support it with the greatest enthusiasm. At the same time, we especially fervently support the government's rapid mobilization of this "morale" of the entire nation, which is at its peak, and "use it while it's hot!"

On the Island

— Lin Na

This island is only about one square mile in size and is shrouded in damp mist year-round.

When the Spanish monarchy ruled these thirty-six islands with priests and the Bible, this place was a penal colony for condemned prisoners. A century later, the ruling power changed, and it remained a penal colony for condemned prisoners. The difference was that the priests then instructed the prisoners about their Queen, but now, no one tells them, though they know themselves to be the people of Roosevelt.

On the island's highest peak stands a fortress-like, grand prison, a building constructed by the prisoners themselves to confine themselves. Outside, dozens of watchtowers are scattered, manned by white-skinned guards. Holding their gun handles, they sit there majestically, gazing at the azure sky and listening to the sea's murmur.

Inside the fortress, the roar of enormous machines echoes day and night, spreading across the entire silent island through the tall walls. This comes from four different prison workshops. Prisoners, dragging their clanging shackles, are herded out of the prison cells in groups when the siren wails, heading to the workshops. There, they must labor, managing the blood-sucking machines. It is said that even ordinary prisoners have this privilege, while political prisoners are deprived of even this small freedom.

Armed guards and foremen dragging light iron chains constantly run among them, brandishing whips. For even a small mistake, these prisoners wearing collarless uniforms and with shaved heads are dragged out to be hung and whipped or nailed to large frames in damp basements. Thus, the weak are visited by death, and the strong must embrace their wounds, laboring for reasons they themselves cannot fathom.

When we, as a group of reporters, boarded a light electric boat, chasing the calm waves of Manila harbor, and were led to this terrifying island, it was already around two o'clock in the afternoon. We passed many cold, desolate fields and prison cells, heading toward the workshops emitting the mechanical noise. This was a narrow, long room that could only accommodate about a hundred people, but it was crammed with about one hundred and fifty. The machines roared with clumsy sounds, mixed with the heat and sweat of empty people, swirling in the turbid space, making one feel heavy and dizzy.

The prisoners were skilled in their work. They worked with excessive efficiency, carefully and quietly, as if afraid of making mistakes or falling behind, for they clearly knew what terrible consequences would ensue.

We stood silently, about to move to the other side, when suddenly, everyone was captivated by a strange phenomenon. In that dark corner, a thin old man fainted. Immediately, he was dragged to an open space, lying on his back, his body convulsing terribly, his forehead sweating, his eyes rolling back, and white foam coming from his mouth. Standing next to him was a tall man dressed as a foreman, dragging light iron chains, wielding a whip in his hand, forcefully lashing at him, murmuring curses:

"Now, let's see if you'll pretend to be dead!"

These foremen are chosen from among the prisoners. They are treated favorably by the prison officials and allowed to have a whip, with which they can arbitrarily lash every weak companion, even though they are also prisoners who must spend their lives on this isolated island.

The workshop immediately became tense, but they dared not stop their work to look at the abused companion. They dared not breathe or utter a sigh of resentment. I stood there, bearing extremely bad feelings, looking at every sweating face. I wanted to understand the extent of their anger. However, what I saw were the same desperate and sorrowful faces. A young man of about twenty even grinned and made a face at me.

"Sir, are you sent from above?" he asked me quietly.

"No, I'm a journalist..." I replied, shaking my head.

"Hmm..." his hands were moving again. "Then, can you give me some cigarettes?" he continued, introducing himself. "My name is Rizal, twenty-two years old, coachman, convicted of murder..."

"Don't you also get paid?" I handed him some leftover cigarillos.

"God only knows how they deduct it. We get less than a dollar a month..." he replied, hiding the cigarettes.

The old man had been carried away. There was a series of crisp leather shoe sounds coming from another corner. He winked at me alertly and then went back to work as if nothing had happened. Then, I also lifted my feet and moved towards the exit.

Returning home, I wrote down the following thoughts with a painful heart: "...The prisoners are living in a bloody and hungry atmosphere. They work more than fourteen hours a day, are abused, and eat extremely poor food..."

The next day, in a prominent position, it was changed as follows:

"...We almost can't believe that it is a prison for condemned criminals. Here, they live no differently from ordinary workers. They work and entertain themselves enthusiastically. It is said that many people even save their wages and send them home..."

I laughed loudly, and the newspaper in my hand turned into pieces of scrap.

Spring Garden Lane

— Shi Dai

When I was in Beiping, I used to enjoy strolling around "Tianqiao." When I got to Tianjin, I became inextricably linked with the "Three No Zone." This time I ran to Hong Kong, thinking there would be no gathering place for lower-class entertainment like Ping and Tianjin to play around in, but the reality shattered my expectations. Hong Kong has a "Wan Chai" area whose liveliness is not inferior to "Tianqiao" and the "Three No Zone." How happy I was when I discovered this place! I no longer climb the rocky "Mount Davis," no longer run into the pine forest and under the banyan trees to savor the lovely gurgling springs, but spend every dusk and evening in the embrace of "Wan Chai." As if freed from restraints, my heart is so comfortable and so happy. The world of "Wan Chai" has no barrier, no hatred with me. The things I see and encounter are all amiable and kind, and most of all, understandable to me.

What interests me most in the "Wan Chai" area is "Spring Garden Lane." It is the central location for lower-class entertainment, especially for laborers. They continuously pour into "Spring Garden Lane" from the docks, from the factories, from the fish and vegetable markets. Once dusk arrives, the liveliness doubles in intensity.

When the streetlights outside the window shine, I take off the wooden clogs that never leave my feet all day, put on rubber-soled shoes, and go out. Across the sea, countless lights sparkle like stars, the calm sea separating Hong Kong and Kowloon. The countless lights on both sides shine brightly, as if enticing each other. The market is noisy, the sound of mahjong fills every place, and even the urgent ringing of the trams cannot drown it out. The yellow-uniformed Indian police officers direct the passing vehicles, so busy that they are covered in sweat. After a short break, they glance at the sumptuous dishes in the restaurants on the side of the street. Under the neon lights, it is not easy to distinguish between Indians and Malays? Why are there so few white people in this colony? Almost all I see are Chinese, Japanese, Filipinos, Malays, and very few Hawaiians. Whether on the street, in the market, or at the dock, besides the Chinese, only Indians are numerous.

Spiritual Pivot and Simple Questions

— Answered by Dr. Liu Xinbai

Difficulty Breathing and Discomfort

No. 116, Shi Yanchang from Tushanwan, Xujiahui, asks: My constitution has always been weak, and because of overwork, I cannot sleep until after midnight. Sometimes, I am suddenly startled awake from a deep sleep, covered in a cold sweat. When lying on my left side, I experience difficulty breathing and discomfort. A friend said it might be heart disease, which has left me distraught. I would like to ask: (1) What is the illness? (2) What medicine should I take?

Answer: It sounds like heart disease, but there are dozens of types of heart disease, and the treatments and prognoses are all different. Based on your letter alone, it is impossible to determine which type of heart disease it is. Prescribing medicine without a proper diagnosis may lead to errors and even danger. Therefore, please get examined first to determine what the illness is. Then, take medicine and recuperate appropriately.

Blurred Night Vision

No. 117, Li Jingzhong asks: My younger sister is only fifteen years old. After 6 PM, she cannot see with both eyes. She says she can only see blurry lights. Even if other objects are placed right in front of her, she cannot see them. But during the day, her vision returns. Therefore, I would like to ask: (1) What is the illness? (2) Is there any medicine that can cure it? (3) What is the cause?

Answer: (1) Night blindness. (2) Nutritional deficiency and neurasthenia. (3) Take "Vitamin A" (Vitamin-A).

Urethral Itching

No. 118, Cheng Xin from Yingxun Road, Nanshi, asks: I was tempted by bad friends to visit prostitutes once. Fifteen days later, my urethra started to itch. Twenty days later, a lump appeared on the inside of my left thigh, and now it is gradually becoming visible. I would like to ask: (1) What is the illness? (2) What medicine is most effective?

Answer: (1) Urethral itching is urethritis. The location "on the inside of my left thigh" is unclear. I don't know if you are referring to the outside of the anus. If so, it is likely hemorrhoids. (2) For urethritis, take "Qingzhuobian" (Citropin). Hemorrhoids require cauterization, which you cannot do yourself. You must consult a doctor.

Erectile Dysfunction

No. 119, Huang Tianjiong from Lane 37, No. 105, Bailinan Road, asks: I am thirty years old and very strong. I can work without feeling tired. My symptoms are headaches, pain in my heart and stomach, and the inability to get an erection. When I do get an erection, it only lasts for a second or two. I am worried about not being able to have children. Therefore, I would like to ask: (1) Is it due to excessive sexual activity? (2) How can I have this illness when I am so strong? (3) What medicine can cure it? (4) Is it hopeless for me to have children?

Answer: (1) Excessive sexual activity can cause this, but there are many other causes besides excessive sexual activity. (2) Since you have headaches, you should be checked for spinal cord disease, diabetes, and neurasthenia. These are the biggest causes of impotence. Heart and stomach pain should be checked for heart disease and stomach disease. Although heart disease and stomach disease are not causes of impotence, they are still undesirable diseases. There are diseases that only weak people contract, and there are diseases that only strong people contract. Your illness is not related to the strength or weakness of your body. Anyone is susceptible. (3) Inject "Polytonin" and undergo electrotherapy. (4) No.

Anal Bleeding

No. 120, Ms. Zhao Zhiying asks: I am only twenty-two years old. At first, my anus felt hot and painful, and I had constipation. I only had a bowel movement once every two or three days, and there was blood in my stool. My symptoms are still the same. I am pale and thin, and I also have headaches, difficulty breathing, and feelings of distress. These symptoms worsen when my anus hurts badly and disappear when my anus doesn't hurt. I would like to ask: (1) What is the illness? (2) How should I treat it? (3) Is it life-threatening? (4) How should I treat the bleeding? (5) Is there a treatment for the headaches, difficulty breathing, and feelings of distress?

Answer: (1) Internal hemorrhoids. (2) Local injection of "Caseobin." (3) No. (4) Take "Sinocalcin" or insert "Adrenalin Suppository" into the anus. (5) This is called "hemorrhoid distress." No treatment is necessary. Once the original illness is cured, it will naturally disappear.

Nosebleeds

No. 121, Qian Chanyuan from Yongmao Steel Company, South Embankment, Zhejiang Road Bridge, asks: I had nosebleeds two years ago, and I am now twenty-two years old. It has been six or seven years. In the first half of last year, I went to a doctor who performed surgery, washing and applying medicine. The bleeding was only from my right nostril, and the doctor focused on my right nostril. The bleeding stopped, but it still happens sometimes. There's really nothing I can do. Now, the inside of my right nostril seems to be blocked, and I can't breathe through it. (1) What is the reason for this? (2) How can I treat it?

Answer: (1) First, examine your nostril for any illness. (2) Lightly insert cotton wool soaked in "Adrenalin" into your nostril. Also, take "Sinocalcin" regularly.

Ear Discharge

No. 122, Zhang Shuzhi asks: My daughter is nine years old and complains of pain in her right ear. She has become deaf, and pus is coming out of her ear. It has not healed despite many treatments. I would like to ask: (1) Is this what is called "red ear"? (2) Is it dangerous? (3) Please tell me the most effective treatment. (4) What is the scientific name?

Answer: Yes, the scientific name is acute suppurative otitis media. (2) Treat it quickly, otherwise it will become mastoiditis (a large blister behind the ear) or turn chronic, which will be difficult to treat. (3) Wash the ear with hydrogen peroxide, dry it with cotton wool, and blow in Haibiform powder. It will heal in a few days. Injecting "Panadin" is also very effective. (4) See (1).

Facial Flushing

No. 123, Lin Yonghui from the International Department of the Telephone Bureau of the Ministry of Communications, Yongxing Road, Zhabei, asks: Every winter, my face suddenly turns red and hot, and my nose also becomes very red. If I feel even slightly irritated at that time, my face becomes even hotter and redder. Once the fever starts, it doesn't go away quickly. This happens more often in the evening than during the day, and it is not related to the winter wind. Sometimes, the fever starts immediately when I eat or after a meal.
